TITLE      Photoneutron reaction cross  sections  in  experiments M063500100003 
            with   beams   of   quasimonoenergetic   annihilation M063500100004 
            photons.                                              M063500100005 
AUTHOR     (V.V.Varlamov,N.N.Peskov,D.S.Rudenko,M.E.Stepanov)     M063500100006 
REFERENCE  (J,YK,2003,(1-2),48,2003)                              M063500100007 
           (R,MSU-INP-2003-2/715,2003)                            M063500100008

ANALYSIS   The typical  differences  between Saclay and Livermore M063500100013 
            data are the following at the same time:              M063500100014 
            - as  a rule total photoneutron reaction (g,xn) cross M063500100015 
              section values (both amplitude and integrated cross M063500100016 
              section  values) obtained  at Livermore are smaller M063500100017 
              and  must  be  multiplied  by  special  coefficient M063500100018 
              (about 5 - 15%);                                    M063500100019 
            - the  (g,n) reaction (in fact - the sum of reactions M063500100020 
              (g,n) + (g,np))  cross section differ both in shape M063500100021 
              and magnitude,   these   of  Livermore  being  much M063500100022 
              smaller;                                            M063500100023 
            - the  (g,2n)  reaction  cross section differ both in M063500100024 
              shape and magnitude,  these of Livermore being much M063500100025 
              bigger.                                             M063500100026 
            Because two  laboratories  data  for  (g,xn) reaction M063500100027 
            cross section obtained without  neutron  multiplicity M063500100028 
            sorting  for  all gamma  energies disagree each other M063500100029 
            by about several percents,  but data  for  (g,n)  and M063500100030 
            (g,2n)  obtained  using neutron multiplicity sorting, M063500100031 
            disagree much more and in opposite sides  (while  the M063500100032 
            integrated (g,n) cross sections form Saclay are about M063500100033 
            40 % bigger than the Livermore data, their integrated M063500100034 
            (g,2n)   reaction  cross  sections  are  about  50  % M063500100035 
            smaller) on the base that Saclay neutron multiplicity M063500100036 
            sorting  procedure was not correct,  the Saclay (g,n) M063500100037 
            and (g,2n) reaction cross section data were modified. M063500100038 
            The equation                                          M063500100039 
             sig-2n-S-mod = sig-2n-S + 1/2*(sig-n-S - R*sig-n-L)  M063500100040 
            gives to  one  the  possibility to obtained evaluated M063500100041 
            (corrected, modified) Saclay cross  section  data  by M063500100042 
            transmitting  back  into  the  (g,2n)  reaction cross M063500100043 
            section  part  of  (g,n)   reaction   cross   section M063500100044 
            incorrectly putted  into  this channel.  The constant M063500100045 
            values R using for each investigated nucleus  in  the M063500100046 
            modification   formula   were   obtained   as  ratios M063500100047 
            (sig-xn-S)/(sig-xn-L) for total photoneutron reaction M063500100048 
            (g,xn)  cross  section  data  obtained  at Saclay and M063500100049 
            Livermore (in good agreement with previously  founded M063500100050 
            for big systematics value R-syst = 1.122 (0.243)).    M063500100051 
            Because the  evaluated  (corrected)   Saclay   (g,2n) M063500100052 
            reaction  cross  section  was  obtained  by  addition M063500100053 
            (moving back) the  "false"  part  of  (g,n)  reaction M063500100054 
            cross section                                         M063500100055 
                            1/2*(sig-n-S - r*sig-n-L)             M063500100056 
            the evaluated (corrected) Saclay (g,n) reaction cross M063500100057 
            section was obtained by subtraction of  that  "false" M063500100058 
            part                                                  M063500100059 
                sig-n-S-mod =  sig-n-S  -  (sig-n-S - r*sig-n-L), M063500100060 
            where part in brackets is calculating in the range of M063500100061 
            energies more  than  (g,2n) reaction threshold,  from M063500100062 
            correspondent (g,n) reaction cross  section  obtained M063500100063 
            at Saclay.                                            M063500100064 
            At the  same  time  Livermore  evaluated data for all M063500100065 
            three kinds of reactions ((g,xn), (g,n),  and (g,2n)) M063500100066 
            were obtained by multiplication by coefficient R.     M063500100067 
REL-REF    (E,,B.S.ISHKHANOV+,C,2001TSUKUB,5-P-6,2001)            M063500100068 
            Systematical   analysis  of  the  total  photoneutron M063500100069 
            reaction (g,xn)  cross  section  values  obtained  at M063500100070 
            various laboratories using different methods.         M063500100071 
           (E,,E.WOLINEC+,J,RBF,17,56,1987) method for correction M063500100072 
            of (g,n)  and  (g,2n)  reaction  cross  section  data M063500100073 
            caused by   the   difference  in  the  analysis  that M063500100074 
            separates the total counts of neutrons into (g,n) and M063500100075 
            (g,2n) events.                                        M063500100076 
ERR-ANALYS (DATA-ERR) Mean root-square errors  are given.         M063500100077 
COMMENT    The accurate system analysis of the (g,xn),  (g,n) and M063500100078 
            (g,2n)  reaction cross section data obtained by using M063500100079 
            quasimonoenergetical  annihilation  photon  beams  at M063500100080 
            Livermore  (USA)  and Saclay (France) was carried out M063500100081 
            for 19 (for 7 - at  first)  nuclei  51V,  75As,  89Y, M063500100082 
            90Zr,   115In,  116,117,118,120,124Sn,  127I,  133Cs, M063500100083 
            159Tb,  165Ho,  181Ta,  197Au, 208Pb, 232Th, 238U. It M063500100084 
            was  observed  that the (g,xn) reaction cross section M063500100085 
            data obtained  at  both  laboratories  without  using M063500100086 
            neutron multiplicity sorting procedure disagree by 10 M063500100087 
            - 15 %.  Additionally  it  was  found  out  that  the M063500100088 
            disagreement  of  partial  reactions (g,n) and (g,2n) M063500100089 
            cross sections,  obtained at both laboratories  using M063500100090 
            neutron    multiplicity    sorting    procedure   are M063500100091 
            significantly more (till 30 - 40 %)  and  as  a  rule M063500100092 
            have  opposite  directions.  These disagreements were M063500100093 
            interpreted as the result of  difference  of  neutron M063500100094 
            multiplicity   sorting   procedures   used   in  both M063500100095 
            laboratories:  that is incorrect at Saclay  with  the M063500100096 
            result  of  uncorrect  transmission  of  the  part of M063500100097 
            (g,2n) reaction cross section into the (g,n) reaction M063500100098 
            cross  section.  The  special method was used to move M063500100099 
            the  data  into  consistence.  Its   idea   is   that M063500100100 
            correspondent  "false"  part  of (g,n) reaction cross M063500100101 
            section is recalculated  and  transmitted  back  into M063500100102 
            (g,2n)  reaction  cross  section.  For  all 19 nuclei M063500100103 
            listed the jointly corrected (g,xn), (g,n) and (g,2n) M063500100104 
            reaction  cross  sections were evaluated and prepared M063500100105 
            for  including  into  the  EXFOR   nuclear   reaction M063500100106 
            database.                                             M063500100107
